    Index stride
)

### function rcond_invmatrix_L1_norm_estimate

```cpp
template <typename Decomposition >
Decomposition::RealScalar rcond_invmatrix_L1_norm_estimate(
    const Decomposition & dec
)
```


**See**: <a href="http://example.org/classes/classeigen_1_1fullpivlu/">FullPivLU</a>, <a href="http://example.org/classes/classeigen_1_1partialpivlu/">PartialPivLU</a>, <a href="http://example.org/classes/classeigen_1_1ldlt/">LDLT</a>, <a href="http://example.org/classes/classeigen_1_1llt/">LLT</a>. 

**Return**: an estimate of ||inv(matrix)||_1 given a decomposition of _matrix_ that implements .solve() and .adjoint().solve() methods.


This function implements Algorithms 4.1 and 5.1 from <a href="http://www.maths.manchester.ac.uk/~higham/narep/narep135.pdf">http://www.maths.manchester.ac.uk/~higham/narep/narep135.pdf</a> which also forms the basis for the condition number estimators in LAPACK. Since at most 10 calls to the solve method of dec are performed, the total cost is O(dims^2), as opposed to O(dims^3) needed to compute the inverse matrix explicitly.

The most common usage is in estimating the condition number ||matrix||_1 * ||inv(matrix)||_1. The first term ||matrix||_1 can be computed directly in O(n^2) operations.

Supports the following decompositions: <a href="http://example.org/classes/classeigen_1_1fullpivlu/">FullPivLU</a>, <a href="http://example.org/classes/classeigen_1_1partialpivlu/">PartialPivLU</a>, <a href="http://example.org/classes/classeigen_1_1ldlt/">LDLT</a>, and <a href="http://example.org/classes/classeigen_1_1llt/">LLT</a>.


### function rcond_estimate_helper

```cpp
template <typename Decomposition >
Decomposition::RealScalar rcond_estimate_helper(
    typename Decomposition::RealScalar matrix_norm,
    const Decomposition & dec
)
```

Reciprocal condition number estimator. 

**See**: <a href="http://example.org/classes/classeigen_1_1fullpivlu/">FullPivLU</a>, <a href="http://example.org/classes/classeigen_1_1partialpivlu/">PartialPivLU</a>, <a href="http://example.org/classes/classeigen_1_1ldlt/">LDLT</a>, <a href="http://example.org/classes/classeigen_1_1llt/">LLT</a>. 

**Return**: an estimate of the reciprocal condition number (1 / (||matrix||_1 * ||inv(matrix)||_1)) of matrix, given ||matrix||_1 and its decomposition. Supports the following decompositions: <a href="http://example.org/classes/classeigen_1_1fullpivlu/">FullPivLU</a>, <a href="http://example.org/classes/classeigen_1_1partialpivlu/">PartialPivLU</a>, <a href="http://example.org/classes/classeigen_1_1ldlt/">LDLT</a>, and <a href="http://example.org/classes/classeigen_1_1llt/">LLT</a>.

Computing a decomposition of a dense matrix takes O(n^3) operations, while this method estimates the condition number quickly and reliably in O(n^2) operations.

### function pstoret

```cpp
template <typename Scalar ,

### function computeProductBlockingSizes

```cpp
template <typename LhsScalar ,
typename RhsScalar ,
int KcFactor,
typename Index >
void computeProductBlockingSizes(
    Index & k,
    Index & m,
    Index & n,
    Index num_threads =1
)
```

Computes the blocking parameters for a m x k times k x n matrix product. 

**Parameters**: 

  * **k** Input: the third dimension of the product. Output: the blocking size along the same dimension. 
  * **m** Input: the number of rows of the left hand side. Output: the blocking size along the same dimension. 
  * **n** Input: the number of columns of the right hand side. Output: the blocking size along the same dimension.


**See**: <a href="http://example.org/namespaces/namespaceeigen/#function-setcpucachesizes">setCpuCacheSizes</a>


Given a m x k times k x n matrix product of scalar types <code>LhsScalar</code> and <code>RhsScalar</code>, this function computes the blocking size parameters along the respective dimensions for matrix products and related algorithms.

The blocking size parameters may be evaluated:

* either by a heuristic based on cache sizes;
* or using fixed prescribed values (for testing purposes).


### function computeProductBlockingSizes

```cpp
template <typename LhsScalar ,
typename RhsScalar ,
typename Index >
inline void computeProductBlockingSizes(
    Index & k,
    Index & m,
    Index & n,
    Index num_threads =1
)
```

### function tridiagonalization_inplace

```cpp
template <typename MatrixType ,
typename CoeffVectorType >
void tridiagonalization_inplace(
    MatrixType & matA,
    CoeffVectorType & hCoeffs
)
```


### function tridiagonalization_inplace

```cpp
template <typename MatrixType ,
typename DiagonalType ,
typename SubDiagonalType >
void tridiagonalization_inplace(
    MatrixType & mat,
    DiagonalType & diag,
    SubDiagonalType & subdiag,
    bool extractQ
)
```

Performs a full tridiagonalization in place. 

**Parameters**: 

  * **mat** On input, the selfadjoint matrix whose tridiagonal decomposition is to be computed. Only the lower triangular part referenced. The rest is left unchanged. On output, the orthogonal matrix Q in the decomposition if <code>extractQ</code> is true. 
  * **diag** The diagonal of the tridiagonal matrix T in the decomposition. 
  * **subdiag** The subdiagonal of the tridiagonal matrix T in the decomposition. 
  * **extractQ** If true, the orthogonal matrix Q in the decomposition is computed and stored in <code>mat</code>.


**See**: class <a href="http://example.org/classes/classeigen_1_1tridiagonalization/">Tridiagonalization</a>

**Note**: Currently, it requires two temporary vectors to hold the intermediate Householder coefficients, and to reconstruct the matrix Q from the Householder reflectors.


Computes the tridiagonal decomposition of the selfadjoint matrix <code>mat</code> in place such that \( mat = Q T Q^* \) where \( Q \) is unitary and \( T \) a real symmetric tridiagonal matrix.

The tridiagonal matrix T is passed to the output parameters <code>diag</code> and <code>subdiag</code>. If <code>extractQ</code> is true, then the orthogonal matrix Q is passed to <code>mat</code>. Otherwise the lower part of the matrix <code>mat</code> is destroyed.

The vectors <code>diag</code> and <code>subdiag</code> are not resized. The function assumes that they are already of the correct size. The length of the vector <code>diag</code> should equal the number of rows in <code>mat</code>, and the length of the vector <code>subdiag</code> should be one left.

This implementation contains an optimized path for 3-by-3 matrices which is especially useful for plane fitting.


Example (this uses the same matrix as the example in Tridiagonalization::Tridiagonalization(const MatrixType&)): ```cpp

```

_Filename: Tridiagonalization_decomposeInPlace.cpp_

 Output: 

```
```

\jacobi_module Applies the clock wise 2D rotation _j_ to the set of 2D vectors of cordinates _x_ and _y:_\( \left ( \begin{array}{cc} x \\ y \end{array} \right )  =  J \left ( \begin{array}{cc} x \\ y \end{array} \right ) \)

    MatrixType & mat,
    typename MatrixType::RealScalar * diagonal,
    typename MatrixType::RealScalar * upper_diagonal,
    typename MatrixType::Scalar * tempData =0
)
```
